five key classes:\\n\\n### 1. WindowAssigner (Abstract Base Class)\\n**Location**: `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/assigners/WindowAssigner.java`\\n\\nThe abstract base class defines the core contract that all window assigners must implement. A developer implementing a custom window assigner must provide implementations for:\\n\\n**Abstract Methods**:\\n- `Collection<W> assignWindows(T element, long timestamp, WindowAssignerContext context)` - Assigns zero or more windows to an element based on its timestamp\\n- `Trigger<T, W> getDefaultTrigger()` - Returns the default trigger associated with this assigner\\n- `TypeSerializer<W> getWindowSerializer(ExecutionConfig executionConfig)` - Provides serialization for windows assigned by this assigner\\n- `boolean isEventTime()` - Returns true if elements are assigned to windows based on event time\\n\\n**Inner Class**:\\n- `WindowAssignerContext` - An abstract context provided by the WindowOperator that allows the assigner to query the current processing time via `long getCurrentProcessingTime()`\\n\\n### 2. MergingWindowAssigner (For Session-Style Windows)\\n**Location**: `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/assigners/MergingWindowAssigner.java`\\n\\nFor window types that support merging (such as session windows), implementations extend `MergingWindowAssigner<T, W>` instead of directly implementing `WindowAssigner`. This adds:\\n\\n**Key Abstract Method**:\\n- `void mergeWindows(Collection<W> windows, MergeCallback<W> callback)` - Determines which windows should be merged. The implementation examines candidate windows and calls `callback.merge()` to signal which windows should merge together.\\n\\n**Inner Interface**:\\n- `MergeCallback<W>` - Used to signal merge results with method `void merge(Collection<W> toBeMerged, W mergeResult)`\\n\\n### 3. Trigger (Event Lifecycle Handler)\\n**Location**: `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/triggers/Trigger.java`\\n\\nWhile not strictly part of the window assigner interface, triggers work in tandem with assigners and define critical lifecycle extension points. A custom assigner's `getDefaultTrigger()` method returns a trigger instance that implements:\\n\\n**Lifecycle Abstract Methods**:\\n- `TriggerResult onElement(T element, long timestamp, W window, TriggerContext ctx)` - Called for every element added to a window pane\\n- `TriggerResult onEventTime(long time, W window, TriggerContext ctx)` - Called when an event-time timer fires\\n- `TriggerResult onProcessingTime(long time, W window, TriggerContext ctx)` - Called when a processing-time timer fires\\n- `void clear(W window, TriggerContext ctx)` - Called to clean up window state when the window is purged\\n\\n**Optional Extension Methods** (for merging window support):\\n- `boolean canMerge()` - Returns true to indicate support for merging (default: false)\\n- `void onMerge(W window, OnMergeContext ctx)` - Called when multiple windows are merged (must be implemented if canMerge() returns true)\\n\\n**Inner Interfaces**:\\n- `TriggerContext` - Provides methods to register timers (`registerEventTimeTimer()`, `registerProcessingTimeTimer()`), manage state (`getPartitionedState()`), and query time (`getCurrentProcessingTime()`, `getCurrentWatermark()`)\\n- `OnMergeContext extends TriggerContext` - Extends TriggerContext with `mergePartitionedState()` for handling state during window merges\\n\\n### 4. EventTimeSessionWindows (Reference Implementation)\\n**Location**: `flink-streaming-java/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/assigners/EventTimeSessionWindows.java`\\n\\nThis concrete implementation demonstrates the pattern for a session window assigner:\\n\\n**Class Declaration**: `public class EventTimeSessionWindows extends MergingWindowAssigner<Object, TimeWindow>`\\n\\n**Key Implementation Details**:\\n- `assignWindows()` - Creates a single `TimeWindow` spanning from the element's timestamp to `timestamp + sessionTimeout`\\n- `mergeWindows()` - Delegates to the static utility method `TimeWindow.mergeWindows()`, which handles merging of overlapping time windows\\n- `getDefaultTrigger()` - Returns `EventTimeTrigger.create()` to fire windows based on event-time progress\\n- `getWindowSerializer()` - Returns `new TimeWindow.Serializer()` for serializing TimeWindow instances\\n- `isEventTime()` - Returns true since session windows are based on event timestamps\\n\\n### 5. TimeWindow (Window Type)\\n**Location**: `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/windows/TimeWindow.java`\\n\\nThe concrete window type that event-time window assigners produce:\\n\\n**Class Declaration**: `public class TimeWindow extends Window`\\n\\n**Constructor**: `TimeWindow(long start, long end)` - Creates a time-based window from start (inclusive) to end (exclusive)\\n\\n**Key Methods**:\\n- `long getStart()` - Returns the inclusive start timestamp\\n- `long getEnd()` - Returns the exclusive end timestamp\\n- `long maxTimestamp()` - Returns the largest timestamp still belonging to this window (equals `end - 1`)\\n- `boolean intersects(TimeWindow other)` - Checks if this window overlaps with another window\\n- `TimeWindow cover(TimeWindow other)` - Returns a minimal window covering both windows\\n- **Static Utility**: `static void mergeWindows(Collection<TimeWindow> windows, MergeCallback<TimeWindow> c)` - Sorts windows by start time and merges all overlapping windows, calling the callback for each merged group\\n\\n**Inner Class**:\\n- `Serializer extends TypeSerializerSingleton<TimeWindow>` - Handles serialization of TimeWindow instances to/from byte format\\n\\n## Summary\\n\\nA developer implementing a custom window assigner must:\\n1. Extend `WindowAssigner<T, W>` (or `MergingWindowAssigner<T, W>` for session-style windows)\\n2. Implement the four abstract methods of WindowAssigner\\n3. For merging assigners, implement the `mergeWindows()` method that determines window merge candidates\\n4. five key classes:\\n\\n### 1. WindowAssigner (Abstract Base Class)\\n**Location**: `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/assigners/WindowAssigner.java`\\n\\nThe abstract base class defines the core contract that all window assigners must implement. A developer implementing a custom window assigner must provide implementations for:\\n\\n**Abstract Methods**:\\n- `Collection<W> assignWindows(T element, long timestamp, WindowAssignerContext context)` - Assigns zero or more windows to an element based on its timestamp\\n- `Trigger<T, W> getDefaultTrigger()` - Returns the default trigger associated with this assigner\\n- `TypeSerializer<W> getWindowSerializer(ExecutionConfig executionConfig)` - Provides serialization for windows assigned by this assigner\\n- `boolean isEventTime()` - Returns true if elements are assigned to windows based on event time\\n\\n**Inner Class**:\\n- `WindowAssignerContext` - An abstract context provided by the WindowOperator that allows the assigner to query the current processing time via `long getCurrentProcessingTime()`\\n\\n### 2. MergingWindowAssigner (For Session-Style Windows)\\n**Location**: `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/assigners/MergingWindowAssigner.java`\\n\\nFor window types that support merging (such as session windows), implementations extend `MergingWindowAssigner<T, W>` instead of directly implementing `WindowAssigner`. This adds:\\n\\n**Key Abstract Method**:\\n- `void mergeWindows(Collection<W> windows, MergeCallback<W> callback)` - Determines which windows should be merged. The implementation examines candidate windows and calls `callback.merge()` to signal which windows should merge together.\\n\\n**Inner Interface**:\\n- `MergeCallback<W>` - Used to signal merge results with method `void merge(Collection<W> toBeMerged, W mergeResult)`\\n\\n### 3. Trigger (Event Lifecycle Handler)\\n**Location**: `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/triggers/Trigger.java`\\n\\nWhile not strictly part of the window assigner interface, triggers work in tandem with assigners and define critical lifecycle extension points. A custom assigner's `getDefaultTrigger()` method returns a trigger instance that implements:\\n\\n**Lifecycle Abstract Methods**:\\n- `TriggerResult onElement(T element, long timestamp, W window, TriggerContext ctx)` - Called for every element added to a window pane\\n- `TriggerResult onEventTime(long time, W window, TriggerContext ctx)` - Called when an event-time timer fires\\n- `TriggerResult onProcessingTime(long time, W window, TriggerContext ctx)` - Called when a processing-time timer fires\\n- `void clear(W window, TriggerContext ctx)` - Called to clean up window state when the window is purged\\n\\n**Optional Extension Methods** (for merging window support):\\n- `boolean canMerge()` - Returns true to indicate support for merging (default: false)\\n- `void onMerge(W window, OnMergeContext ctx)` - Called when multiple windows are merged (must be implemented if canMerge() returns true)\\n\\n**Inner Interfaces**:\\n- `TriggerContext` - Provides methods to register timers (`registerEventTimeTimer()`, `registerProcessingTimeTimer()`), manage state (`getPartitionedState()`), and query time (`getCurrentProcessingTime()`, `getCurrentWatermark()`)\\n- `OnMergeContext extends TriggerContext` - Extends TriggerContext with `mergePartitionedState()` for handling state during window merges\\n\\n### 4. EventTimeSessionWindows (Reference Implementation)\\n**Location**: `flink-streaming-java/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/assigners/EventTimeSessionWindows.java`\\n\\nThis concrete implementation demonstrates the pattern for a session window assigner:\\n\\n**Class Declaration**: `public class EventTimeSessionWindows extends MergingWindowAssigner<Object, TimeWindow>`\\n\\n**Key Implementation Details**:\\n- `assignWindows()` - Creates a single `TimeWindow` spanning from the element's timestamp to `timestamp + sessionTimeout`\\n- `mergeWindows()` - Delegates to the static utility method `TimeWindow.mergeWindows()`, which handles merging of overlapping time windows\\n- `getDefaultTrigger()` - Returns `EventTimeTrigger.create()` to fire windows based on event-time progress\\n- `getWindowSerializer()` - Returns `new TimeWindow.Serializer()` for serializing TimeWindow instances\\n- `isEventTime()` - Returns true since session windows are based on event timestamps\\n\\n### 5. TimeWindow (Window Type)\\n**Location**: `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/windows/TimeWindow.java`\\n\\nThe concrete window type that event-time window assigners produce:\\n\\n**Class Declaration**: `public class TimeWindow extends Window`\\n\\n**Constructor**: `TimeWindow(long start, long end)` - Creates a time-based window from start (inclusive) to end (exclusive)\\n\\n**Key Methods**:\\n- `long getStart()` - Returns the inclusive start timestamp\\n- `long getEnd()` - Returns the exclusive end timestamp\\n- `long maxTimestamp()` - Returns the largest timestamp still belonging to this window (equals `end - 1`)\\n- `boolean intersects(TimeWindow other)` - Checks if this window overlaps with another window\\n- `TimeWindow cover(TimeWindow other)` - Returns a minimal window covering both windows\\n- **Static Utility**: `static void mergeWindows(Collection<TimeWindow> windows, MergeCallback<TimeWindow> c)` - Sorts windows by start time and merges all overlapping windows, calling the callback for each merged group\\n\\n**Inner Class**:\\n- `Serializer extends TypeSerializerSingleton<TimeWindow>` - Handles serialization of TimeWindow instances to/from byte format\\n\\n## Summary\\n\\nA developer implementing a custom window assigner must:\\n1. Extend `WindowAssigner<T, W>` (or `MergingWindowAssigner<T, W>` for session-style windows)\\n2. Implement the four abstract methods of WindowAssigner\\n3. For merging assigners, implement the `mergeWindows()` method that determines window merge candidates\\n4. Provide a `getDefaultTrigger()` that returns a `Trigger` implementation controlling when windows fire\\n5. Define or reuse a window type (like `TimeWindow`) extending `Window`\\n\\nThe EventTimeSessionWindows class exemplifies this pattern: it assigns elements to session windows, merges overlapping sessions, uses event-time triggers, and produces TimeWindow instances that track time intervals.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
